(b) **No standing limit-sell order at the notional trigger** — would not have helped here (limit at ~$443 would have failed to fill on a gap-down to $410), but for asymmetric gap-down scenarios, a stop-LIMIT might have provided more control. On today's case: a stop-LIMIT with trigger $443 / limit $410 would have allowed the $410.57 fill we got; a stop-LIMIT with trigger $443 / limit $430 would have NOT filled (preventing the loss but leaving the position exposed) — neither is unambiguously better. Today's HOLD on AVGO is a textbook case.

(c) **Cash-drag cost asymmetry materialized today** — first negative-alpha day of Week 2 was −0.85%, which is larger in magnitude than either of the two positive-alpha days (+0.16% Mon, +0.52% Tue). This is the inherent asymmetry of holding 97.9% cash: small wins on down-days, larger gives on big up-days. Cumulative Week 2 alpha is still net positive on a 2-up-1-down ratio but the realized alpha drop today is a real datapoint to log.
- **One thing to try differently next time**: when SPY moves >+0.5% on a day that includes a scheduled binary catalyst (FOMC minutes), explicitly compute the alpha-drag in absolute dollars (today: −0.85% × $100,001.55 = −$850 of *forgone* return vs full SPY exposure) and weigh that against the *avoided* tail-risk (a hawkish surprise could have driven SPY −2%; we'd have *gained* +2% alpha). This is the structural insurance trade-off being made by the cash sleeve — quantifying it on both up-days and down-days produces a fairer cumulative picture than just tracking realized alpha.
- **Lesson / Heuristic**: **Alpha is asymmetric for cash-heavy portfolios — track the dollar magnitude of forgone-vs-captured alpha on each side, not just signed alpha.** Today: forgone +$850 on a +0.89% SPY up-day (we'd have captured this at full exposure). Mon: captured +$160 alpha on a −0.16% SPY day. Tue: captured +$520 alpha on a −0.52% SPY day. Week 2 net dollar alpha: +$160 + $520 − $850 = **−$170 dollar-weighted** through Wed close, even though signed-percent alpha is still net positive (a function of small base values × small percentages). The percent-alpha framing can flatter cash sleeves; dollar-alpha is the honest measure. **Heuristic added**: at every close session, compute both signed-percent-alpha AND dollar-alpha (signed_pct × prior_close_equity) for the day, and the running dollar-alpha for the week — this is the cleanest measure of whether discipline cost or saved real money.

The position only achieves a positive-P&L floor when AVGO trades >$456.66; below that, the stop protects against drawdown but doesn't lock in profit. This number frames every session's progress against a *concrete target* (close-of-day price vs $456.66 = "how close to lock-in?").
